  <h1 itemprop="name" class="devsite-page-title">
    Getting Started
  </h1>
  
  
  <nav class="devsite-page-nav-embedded devsite-nav"></nav>
  
  <div class="devsite-article-body clearfix
            "
       itemprop="articleBody">
    


<h2 id="Audience">Audience</h2>

<p>This documentation is designed for people familiar with
  <a href="http://www.ecma-international.org/publications/standards/Ecma-262.htm">
    JavaScript</a> programming and object-oriented programming concepts. You
    should also be familiar with <a href="https://maps.google.com/">Google
      Maps</a> from a user's point of view. There are many
    <a href="https://www.google.com/search?q=javascript+tutorials">JavaScript
      tutorials</a> available on the Web.</p>

<p>This conceptual documentation is designed to let you quickly start
  exploring and developing applications with the Google Maps JavaScript API. We also
  publish the <a href="https://developers.google.com/maps/documentation/javascript/reference">Google Maps JavaScript API Reference</a>.</p>

<a name="HelloWorld"></a>
<h2 id="The_Hello_World_of_Google_Maps_v3">Hello, World</h2>

<p>The easiest way to start learning about the Google Maps JavaScript API is to see a
  simple example. The following web page displays a map centered on Sydney, New
  South Wales, Australia:</p>

<div class="devsite-jsfiddle-code-sample devsite-jsfiddle-hide" data-scope="map-simple">
  <pre data-type="js">var map;
function initMap() {
  map = new google.maps.Map(document.getElementById(&#39;map&#39;), {
    center: {lat: -34.397, lng: 150.644},
    zoom: 8
  });
}</pre>
  <pre data-type="html">&lt;div id=&quot;map&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt;</pre>
  <pre data-type="css">/* Always set the map height explicitly to define the size of the div
 * element that contains the map. */
#map {
  height: 100%;
}
/* Optional: Makes the sample page fill the window. */
html, body {
  height: 100%;
  margin: 0;
  padding: 0;
}</pre>
  <pre data-type="html">&lt;!-- Replace the value of the key parameter with your own API key. --&gt;
&lt;script src=&quot;https://maps.googleapis.com/maps/api/js?key=AIzaSyCkUOdZ5y7hMm0yrcCQoCvLwzdM6M8s5qk&amp;callback=initMap&quot; async defer&gt;&lt;/script&gt;</pre>
</div>

<pre class="prettyprint notranslate lang-html devsite-enable-open-in-jsfiddle" data-scope="map-simple" data-jsfiddle-title="Map Simple">&lt;!DOCTYPE html&gt;
&lt;html&gt;
  &lt;head&gt;
    &lt;title&gt;Simple Map&lt;/title&gt;
    &lt;meta name=&quot;viewport&quot; content=&quot;initial-scale=1.0&quot;&gt;
    &lt;meta charset=&quot;utf-8&quot;&gt;
    &lt;style&gt;
      /* Always set the map height explicitly to define the size of the div
       * element that contains the map. */
      #map {
        height: 100%;
      }
      /* Optional: Makes the sample page fill the window. */
      html, body {
        height: 100%;
        margin: 0;
        padding: 0;
      }
    &lt;/style&gt;
  &lt;/head&gt;
  &lt;body&gt;
    &lt;div id=&quot;map&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
    &lt;script&gt;
      var map;
      function initMap() {
        map = new google.maps.Map(document.getElementById(&#39;map&#39;), {
          center: {lat: -34.397, lng: 150.644},
          zoom: 8
        });
      }
    &lt;/script&gt;
    &lt;script src=&quot;https://maps.googleapis.com/maps/api/js?key=<var class="apiparam replaceable-credential">YOUR_API_KEY</var>&amp;callback=initMap&quot;
    async defer&gt;&lt;/script&gt;
  &lt;/body&gt;
&lt;/html&gt;
</pre>

<p><a href="https://developers.google.com/maps/documentation/javascript/examples/map-simple">View example
  (map-simple.html)</a></p>

<p>Even in this simple example, there are a few things to note:</p>
<ol>
  <li>We declare the application as HTML5 using the <code>&lt;!DOCTYPE
    html&gt;</code> declaration.</li>
  <li>We create a <code>div</code> element named "map" to hold the
    Map.</li>
  <li>We define a JavasScript function that creates a map in the
    <code>div</code>.</li>
  <li>We load the Maps JavaScript API using a <code>script</code> tag.</li>
</ol>

<p>These steps are explained below.</p>

<h2 id="HTML5">Declaring Your Application as HTML5</h2>

<p>We recommend that you declare a true <code>DOCTYPE</code>
  within your web application. Within the examples here, we've
  declared our applications as HTML5 using the simple HTML5 <code>DOCTYPE</code>
  as shown below:</p>

<pre class="prettyprint notranslate lang-html">
&lt;!DOCTYPE html&gt;
</pre>

<p>Most current browsers will render content that is declared with this
  <code>DOCTYPE</code> in "standards mode" which means that your application
  should be more cross-browser compliant. The <code>DOCTYPE</code> is also
  designed to degrade gracefully; browsers that don't understand it will ignore
  it, and use "quirks mode" to display their content.</p>

<p>Note that some CSS that works within quirks mode is not valid in
standards mode. In specific, all percentage-based sizes must inherit
from parent block elements, and if any of those ancestors fail to
specify a size, they are assumed to be sized at 0 x 0 pixels. For
that reason, we include the following <code>&lt;style&gt;</code>
declaration:</p>

<pre class="prettyprint notranslate lang-html">
&lt;style&gt;
  #map {
    height: 100%;
  }
  html, body {
    height: 100%;
    margin: 0;
    padding: 0;
  }
&lt;/style&gt;
</pre>

<p>This CSS declaration indicates that the map container
  <code>&lt;div&gt;</code>
  (with id <code>map</code>) should take up 100% of the height of the HTML
  body. Note that we must specifically declare those percentages for
  <code>&lt;body&gt;</code> and <code>&lt;html&gt;</code> as well.</p>

<h2 id="Loading_the_Maps_API">Loading the Google Maps JavaScript API</h2>

To load the Google Maps JavaScript API, use a <code>script</code> tag like the one in the
following example:

<pre class="prettyprint notranslate lang-html">
    &lt;script async defer
      src="https://maps.googleapis.com/maps/api/js?key=<var class="apiparam replaceable-credential">YOUR_API_KEY</var>&amp;callback=initMap"&gt;
    &lt;/script&gt;
</pre>

<p>The URL contained in the <code>script</code> tag is the location of a
  JavaScript file that loads all of the symbols and definitions you need for
  using the Maps JavaScript API. This <code>script</code> tag is required.</p>

<p>The <code>async</code> attribute lets the browser render the rest of your
  website while the Maps JavaScript API loads. When the API is ready, it will
  call the  function specified using the <code>callback</code> parameter.</p>

<p>The <code>key</code> parameter contains your application's API key. See
  <a href="https://developers.google.com/maps/documentation/javascript/get-api-key">Get a Key</a> for more information.</p>

<p><strong>Note: Google Maps APIs Premium Plan</strong> customers may use
  either an API key or a valid client ID when loading the API. Get more
  information on
  <a href="https://developers.google.com/maps/documentation/javascript/get-api-key#premium-auth">authentication parameters for
  Premium Plan customers</a>.</p>

<h3>HTTPS or HTTP</h3>

<p>We think security on the web is pretty important, and recommend using HTTPS
  whenever possible. As part of our efforts to make the web more secure, we've
  made all of the Maps JavaScript API available over HTTPS. Using HTTPS
  encryption  makes your site more secure, and more resistant to snooping or tampering.</p>

<p>We recommend loading the Maps JavaScript API over HTTPS using the
  <code>&lt;script&gt;</code> tag provided above.</p>

<p>If required, you can load the Maps JavaScript API over HTTP by
  requesting <code>http://maps.googleapis.com/</code>, or
  <code>http://maps.google.cn</code> for users in China.</p>

<h3 id="libraries">Libraries</h3>

<p>When loading the Maps JavaScript API via the URL you may optionally
  load additional <em>libraries</em> through use of the
  <code>libraries</code> URL parameter. Libraries are modules of code that
  provide additional functionality to the main Maps JavaScript API but are not
  loaded unless you specifically request them. For more
  information, see <a href="https://developers.google.com/maps/documentation/javascript/libraries">
  Libraries in the Maps JavaScript API</a>.</p>

<h3 id="sync">Synchronously Loading the API</h3>
<p>In the <code>script</code> tag that loads the Maps JavaScript API,
  it is possible to  omit the <code>async</code> attribute and the <code>callback</code>
  parameter. This will cause the loading of the API to block until the API is
  downloaded.</p>

<p>This will probably slow your page load. But it means you can write
  subsequent script tags assuming that the API is already loaded.</p>

<h2 id="Map_DOM_Elements">Map DOM Elements</h2>

<pre class="prettyprint notranslate lang-html">
&lt;div id="map"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
</pre>

<p>For the map to display on a web page, we must reserve a spot for it.
  Commonly, we do this by creating a named <code>div</code> element and
  obtaining a reference to this element in the browser's document object model
  (DOM).</p>

<p>In the example above, we used CSS to set the height of the map div to
  "100%". This will expand to fit the size on mobile devices. You may need to
  adjust the width and height values based on the browser's screensize and
  padding. Note that divs usually take their width from their containing
  element, and empty divs usually have 0 height. For this reason, you must
  always set a height on the <code>&lt;div&gt;</code> explicitly.</p>

<h2 id="MapOptions">Map Options</h2>

<p>There are two required options for every map: <code>center</code> and
  <code>zoom</code>.</p>

<pre class="prettyprint notranslate lang-javascript">
map = new google.maps.Map(document.getElementById('map'), {
  center: {lat: -34.397, lng: 150.644},
  zoom: 8
});
</pre>

<h3>Zoom Levels</h3>

<p>The initial resolution at which to display the map is set by the
  <code>zoom</code> property, where zoom <code>0</code>
  corresponds to a map of the Earth fully zoomed out, and larger zoom levels
  zoom in at a higher resolution. Specify zoom level as an integer.</p>
<pre class="prettyprint notranslate lang-javascript">
zoom: 8
</pre>

<p>Offering a map of the entire Earth as a single image would either
  require an immense map, or a small map with very low resolution. As
  a result, map images within Google Maps and the Maps JavaScript API
  are broken up into map "tiles" and "zoom levels." At low zoom levels, a small set of
  map tiles covers a wide area; at higher zoom levels, the tiles are of
  higher resolution and cover a smaller area. The following list shows the
  approximate level of detail you can expect to see at each zoom level:</p>

<ul>
  <li>1: World</li>
  <li>5: Landmass/continent</li>
  <li>10: City</li>
  <li>15: Streets</li>
  <li>20: Buildings</li>
</ul>

<p>The following three images reflect the same location of Tokyo
 at zoom levels 0, 7 and 18.</p>

<p>
  <img src="https://developers.google.com/maps/documentation/javascript/images/tokyo-zoom-0.png" width="200px" />
  <img src="https://developers.google.com/maps/documentation/javascript/images/tokyo-zoom-7.png" width="200px" />
  <img src="https://developers.google.com/maps/documentation/javascript/images/tokyo-zoom-18.png" width="200px" />
</p>

<p>For information on how the Maps JavaScript API loads tiles based on the
current zoom level, see
<a href="https://developers.google.com/maps/documentation/javascript/maptypes#TileCoordinates">
Tile Coordinates</a> in the Map Types documentation.</p>

<h2 id="google.maps.Map">The Map Object</h2>

<pre class="prettyprint notranslate lang-javascript">
map = new google.maps.Map(document.getElementById("map"), {...});
</pre>

<p>The JavaScript class that represents a map is the <code>Map</code> class.
  Objects of this class define a single map on a page. (You may create more
  than one instance of this class &mdash; each object will define a separate
  map on the page.) We create a new instance of this class using the JavaScript
  <code>new</code> operator.</p>

<p>When you create a new map instance, you specify a <code>&lt;div&gt;</code>
  HTML element in the page as a container for the map. HTML nodes
  are children of the JavaScript <code>document</code> object, and
  we obtain a reference to this element via the
  <code>document.getElementById()</code> method.</p>

<p>This code defines a variable (named <code>map</code>) and assigns that
  variable to a new <code>Map</code> object. The function <code>Map()</code> is
  known as a <i>constructor</i> and its definition is shown below:</p>

<table>
  <tr>
    <th>Constructor</th>
    <th>Description</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td><code>Map(mapDiv:Node, opts?:<a href="#MapOptions"><em>MapOptions</em>
      </a>)</code></td>
    <td>Creates a new map inside of the given HTML container &mdash; which is
      typically a DIV element &mdash; using any (optional) parameters that
      are passed.</td>
  </tr>
</table>

<h2 id="Troubleshooting">Troubleshooting</h2>

<aside class="note"><strong>Note:</strong> The <code>sensor</code> parameter
  is no longer required.</aside>

<p>To help you get your maps code up and running,
  <a href="https://plus.google.com/114280001108380956660">Brendan Kenny</a>
  and <a href="https://plus.google.com/+ManoMarks">Mano Marks</a> point out
  some common mistakes and how to fix them in this video.</a>

<div class="video-wrapper">
  <iframe class="devsite-embedded-youtube-video" data-video-id="21PDd17dnnI"
          data-autohide="1" data-showinfo="0"
          frameborder="0" allowfullscreen>
  </iframe>
</div>

<p>If your code isn't working:</p>

<ul>
  <li>Look for typos. Remember that JavaScript is a case-sensitive
    language.</li>
  <li>Check the basics - some of the most common problems occur with the
    initial map creation. Such as:
     <ul>
       <li>Confirm that you've specified the <code>zoom</code>
       and <code>center</code> properties in your map
       options.</li>
       <li>Ensure that you have declared a div element in which the map will
       appear on the screen.</li>
       <li>Ensure that the div element for the map has a height. By default,
       div elements are created with a height of 0, and are therefore
       invisible.</li>
     </ul>
     Refer to our examples for a
     <a href="https://developers.google.com/maps/documentation/javascript/examples/map-simple">reference
     implementation</a>.
  </li>
  <li>Use a JavaScript debugger to help identify problems, like the one available
  in the <a href="https://developers.google.com/chrome-developer-tools/docs/javascript-debugging">Chrome
  Developer Tools</a>. Start by looking in the JavaScript console for errors.
  </li>
  <li>Post questions to <a
  href="https://stackoverflow.com/questions/ask?tags=google-maps-api-3,google-maps">Stack
  Overflow</a>. Guidelines on how to post great questions are available on
  the <a href="https://developers.google.com/maps/support/">Support</a> page.</li>
</ul>
  
  </div>
